+Jamison Brereton

85
Maruts
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
12 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 5, 12
A typical Marut hymn: their beauty and their adornments, their unruly journey to the sacrifice and the thunderstorm it represents, their parentage (Rudra as father, Pr╠е┼Ыni the cow as mother), their fearsome power. One stylistic peculiarity is the ten dency to repeat with minimal variation parts of one verse in the next, an example of concatenative repetition; see 2c/3ab; 4cd/5a; 6c/7b, d; 10a/11a.
Although the focus throughout is firmly on the Maruts, there is one seemingly intrusive verse (9), where the Maruts are unmentioned and mythologically irrel evant, in which Tvaс╣гс╣нar fashions the mace for Indra to slay Vr╠еtra. IndraтАЩs release of the waters after the slaying must be the point of contact, since the next two verses (10тАУ11) concern the MarutsтАЩ tipping the heavenly well to pour out its water.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts On the concatenative repetition in this hymn, see published introduction.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts who are going forth decorate themselves like feminine les; they are gliders (through the air), the sons of Rudra, and doers of good works by which they promote the welfare of earth and heaven; heroes, who grind (solid rocks), they delight in sacrifices.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those who go forth in beauty like wives, spanned together on their journey, the sons of Rudra, possessing wondrous powerтАФ
for the Maruts made the two world-halves grow strongтАФthe heroes reach exhilaration, eager at the rites.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Because of the frequent association of the root тИЪ┼Ыu(m)bh with verbs of motion, esp. тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ (cf., e.g., nearby I.88.2 ┼Ыubh├й k├бс╣Г y─Бnti and cmpds ┼Ыubhaс╣Г-y─Б╠Б(van- )), I interpret pr├б тАж ┼Ы├║mbhante more dynamically than most tr. (e.g., Geldner тАЬDie sich wie Frauen sch├╢n machenтАжтАЭ), esp. given y─Б╠Бman in the same clause.

The connection of the relative clause in p─Бda a with its presumed main clause in d is interrupted by the h├н clause in c. Geldner convincingly suggests that the h├н clause gives an explanation or exemplification of the тАЬwondrous powerтАЭ attributed to them in the last word of b, sud├бс╣Гsasaс╕е, and he is followed by most tr. including me.

This clause contains a periphrastic causative cakrir├й vс╣Ыdh├й with a medial perfect as its base (see Zehnder, Das periphrastische Kausativ im Vedischen, pp. 23, 50-51). Although there is no doubt that the construction is a periphrasis, the reason for its use is unclear. As Zehnder points out (pp. 23, 51), the imperfect of the well- attested morphological causative occurs with just this object in VIII.12.7 y├бt тАж r├│das─л ├бvardhayat. The context here, which contains two present indicatives (┼Ы├║mbhante a, m├бdanti d), does not call for a perfect. I suspect (but cannot demonstrate) that the use of this periphrasis with the perfect has something to do with the middle voice of cakrir├й, which is also apparently unmotivated in the periphrastic construction, and that there is an underlying pun – on rodas─л╠Б, the consort of the Maruts – namely тАЬthe Maruts made the two worlds/*Rodas─л their ownтАЭ (r├│das─л тАж cakrir├й), which would require a medial form. Since, as I demonstrated long ago (тАЬVoice Fluctuation in the Rig Veda: Medial 3rd Plural -anta in Active ParadigmsтАЭ IIJ 21 [1979]), 3rd pl. medial secondary forms in -anta to -├бya-formations are almost universally interpretable as re-marked actives in -an, using *avardhayanta here would not allow the proposed double reading, with a true medial value in the pun. A different pun is also possibly latent here, involving a reflexive reading of the middle: тАЬthey made themselves grow strongтАЭ (cakrir├й vс╣Ыdh├й). This interpretation would feed naturally into the beginning of verse 2: t├б ukс╣гit─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАЬonce grown,тАЭ and 7a t├й тАШvardhanta sv├бtavaso mahitvan─Б╠БтАЬThose self-powerful ones strengthened themselves in their greatnessтАЭ would echo this reflexive interpretation. In both of these suggested puns, one of the words in the p─Бda has to be ignored (vс╣Ыdh├й in the first, r├│das─л in the second), but the suggestive if partial phraseology in both cases would resonate with the audience.

It is also worth noting (though I donтАЩt quite know what to do with this fact) that of the fifteen occurrences of cakrir├й / cakrire in the RV, four of them are found in this hymn (vss. 2, 7, 10 in addition to this one), a strikingly large percentage. And that the three finite verbs in vs. 2 are all medial 3rd pl. with strong subject involvement: p─Бda a mahim─Б╠Бnam ─Б┼Ыata тАЬobtained (their own) greatness,тАЭ b cakrire s├бdaс╕е тАЬmade (their own) seat,тАЭ and c ├бdhi ┼Ыr├нyo dadhire тАЬput on (their own) splendours.тАЭ

+Griffith

THEY who are glancing forth, like women, on their way, doers of mighty deeds, swift racers, Rudra’s Sons,
The Maruts have made heaven and earth increase and grow: in sacrifices they delight, the strong and wild.

+Geldner

Die sich wie Frauen sch├╢n machen, die Gespanne auf der Fahrt, die guteswirkenden Rudras├╢hne - denn die Marut haben beide Welten hochgebracht - die M├дnner berauschen sich an den weisen Reden, darauf begierig.

+Grassmann

Des Rudra S├╢hne, die an Wunderthaten reich auf ihrer Fahrt sch├╢n prangen wie gescharte Fraun, Die Maruts sind’s, die Erd’ und Himmel segneten, die lust’gen Helden freuen bei den Festen sich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey, inaugurated by the gods, have attained majesty; the sons of Rudra have established their dwelling above the sky; glorify him (Indra) who merits to be glorified, they have inspired him with vigour; the sons of Pс╣Ы┼Ыni have acquired dominion.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Utс╣гit─Бsaс╕е = were sprinkled with holy water by the gods: devair-abhiс╣гiktaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Once grown, they attained greatness: the Rudras made their seat in heaven. Chanting their chant, generating IndraтАЩs strength, they whose mother is Pr╠е┼Ыni put on their splendors.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the verbs in this verse, see final comments on vs. 1.

+Griffith

Grown to their perfect strength greatness have they attained; the Rudras have established their abode in heaven.
Singing their song of praise and generating might, they have put glory on, the Sons whom Prsni bare.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the sonf of earth embellish themselves with ornaments, they shine resplendent in their person ns with (brilliant) decorations; they keep aloof every adversary; the waters follow their path.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Gom─Бtaraс╕е, having for their mother the cow (sons of earth)

+Jamison Brereton

When those whose mother is a cow beautify themselves with unguents, the beautiful ones put radiant (ornaments) on their bodies.
They thrust away every antagonist. Ghee flows along their tracks.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The pf. dadhire of b is not in harmony with the three pres. forms, ┼Ыubh├бyante a, b─Б╠Бdhante b, r─лyate c; in particular, the tenses of the subordinate-main clause dyad in ab clash: тАЬwhen they beautify themselves тАж, they have put on тАжтАЭ (The tr. avoids the clash by using simply тАШputтАЩ, ambiguous between present and past in English, but the Sanskrit is not so amenable.) It is difficult to wring a stative/resulative meaning (тАЬthey have put on and now have on тАжтАЭ) out of dadhire, esp. given the identical form in preterital use in 2d. It may be best to assume that dadhire here just echoes the form in 2d, though it might be worth noting that the 3rd pl. mid. present indicative to the redupl. pres., d├бdhate, which we might expect here, is quite rare. However, there is another possible solution to this clash. The pres. ┼Ыubh├бyante in the y├бd clause in p─Бda a appears before vowel-initial a├▒j├нbhiс╕е in the cadence, with, as is usual, the final

-e scanning short in hiatus (that is, probably as *-ay ). It is possible that the underlying form of the verb was actually the injunctive *┼Ыubh├бyanta and that the primary ending

-ante was substituted editorially to prevent the redactional contraction that might have resulted (*┼Ыubh├бyant─Б├▒j├нbhiс╕е). This would allow a past-time reading of the first hemistich, тАЬWhen they beautified themselves тАж, they put on тАжтАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey who are worthily worshipped shine with various weapons; incapable of being overthrown, they are the over-throwers (of mountains); Maruts, swift as thought, entrusted with the duty of sending rain, yoke the spotted deer to your cars.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those good battlers who flash out with their spears, stirring forth even the unstirrable by their powerтАФ
When, o Maruts, in a bullish troop you have yoked the mind-swift
dappled mares to your chariots,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse contains no main clause, just two different subordinate clauses introduced by y├й (ab) and y├бd (cd) respectively, with the first couched in the 3rd ps., the second in the 2nd ps. Although such switches of person in the middle of a verse are far from rare in the RV (see in fact vs. 5), in this case it seems best to consider the first half of this verse a pendant to vs. 3 (also in the 3rd ps.) and the second half an anticipation of vs. 5 (also in the 2nd ps.), esp. since 5a is an abbreviated duplicate of 4cd.

The adj. manoj├║vaс╕е тАШmind-swiftтАЩ could equally well be a nom. pl. masc.

modifying the Maruts or an acc. pl. fem. modifying pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─лс╕е. Most tr. opt for the latter, I think correctly on thematic grounds, but grammatically and semantically either is possible. Grassmann and Macdonell (Vedic Reader) take it as a nominative; certainly its position right before marutaс╕е in p─Бda a, with p┼Хс╣гat─лс╕е appearing only in the middle of the second p─Бda, suggests that the initial audience interpretation would be as a modifier of the Maruts.

+Griffith

When, mighty Warriors, ye who glitter with your spears, o’erthrowing with your strength e’en what is ne’er o’erthrown,
When, O ye Maruts, ye the host that send the rain, had harnessed to your cars the thought-fleet spotted deer.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen, Maruts, urging on the cloud, for the sake of (providing) food, you have yoked the deer to your chariots, the drops fall from the radiant (sun), and moisten the earth, like a hide, with water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aruс╣гa = radiant (applied to the sun or to the Agni of lightning, a harbinger of rain

+Jamison Brereton

When you have yoked the dappled mares to your chariots, speeding the stone at the prize-contest, o MarutsтАФ
they unloose the streams of the ruddy one and inundate the earth with waters like a skin.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted ad vs. 4, the person changes from 2nd to 3rd in the middle of this verse. But this is not the only disruption: the main clause of 5cd begins with ut├б, which has nothing to conjoin. Klein (DGRV I: 451) is puzzled and suggests, somewhat desperately, that the ut├б тАЬfocuses on and emphasizes the second action of the Maruts.тАЭ This seems to open the usage of ut├б unacceptably wide. It is possible instead to see it as an example of тАЬinverse ut├б,тАЭ conjoining the actions of the two clauses of cd, with the parallel verbs v├н с╣гyanti and vy undanti (so also explicitly Macdonell, Reader). Or it may be signaling the resumption of 3rd ps. discourse after the 2nd ps.

intrusions of 4cd-5ab.

The inundation of the skin in p─Бda 4 presumably refers to the wetting of hides in the tanning process (so Geldner).

+Griffith

When ye have harnessed to your cars the spotted deer, urging the thunderbolt, O Maruts, to the fray,
Forth rush the torrents of the dark red stormy cloud, and moisten, like a skin, the earth with water-floods.

+Geldner

Wenn ihr an den Wagen die Antilopen geschirrt habt, w├дhrend ihr Marut im Wettlauf den Stein mitlaufen lasset, dann entfesseln sie auch die Strahlen des r├╢tlichen Rosses. Wie ein Fell begie├Яen sie die Erde mit Wasser.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet your quick-paced, smooth-gliding coursers bear you (hither); and moving swiftly, come with your hands (filled with good things); sit, Maruts, upon the broad seat of sacred grass, and regale yourselves with the sweet sacrificial food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let the quick-streaming spans convey you hither; quickly flying with your arms, go forth.
Sit on the ritual grass: a broad seat has been made for you. Make
yourselves exhilarated, Maruts, on the honeyed stalk.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In vs. 1 the Maruts were themselves called s├бptayaс╕е тАШspansтАЩ, but here that image is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by separating the Maruts from the spans of draught animals that bring them here.

The two raghu- cmpds. pick up raс╣Гh├бyantaс╕е in 5b.

The phrase ur├║ vaс╕е s├бdas kс╣Ыt├бm could technically be in apposition to barh├нс╕е and hence accusative – тАЬSit on the barhis, the broad seat made for youтАЭ – but none of the standard tr. so render it. The position of the vaс╕е favors, but does not impose, this nominal sentence interpretation. For another reason supporting a separation into two clauses see comm. ad I.85.7.

The seat made for the Maruts on the ritual ground is here contrasted with the one they made for themselves in heaven in 2b (div├н тАж ├бdhi cakrire s├бdaс╕е), which event is then repeated in the next verse, 7b ur├║ cakrire s├бdaс╕е, though there the seat is in/on/above the тАЬvaultтАЭ (n─Б╠Бkam).

+Griffith

Let your swift-gliding coursers bear you hitherward with their fleet pinions. Come ye forward with your arms.
Sit on the grass; a wide seat hath been made for you: delight yourselves, O Maruts, in the pleasant food.

+Geldner

Euch sollen die schnellaufenden Gespanne herfahren; mit den Armen schnellfliegend gehet vorw├дrts! Setzet euch auf das Barhis; ein breiter Sitz ist euch bereitet. Berauschet euch, ihr Marut, am s├╝├Яen Somatrank!

+Grassmann

Euch fahre her das hurtig laufende Gespann, schnellfliegend kommet her zu uns mit starkem Arm, Setzt auf die Streu euch, weit ist euch der Sitz gemacht, berauschet euch, o Maruts, an dem s├╝ssen Trank.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬConfiding in their own strength, they have increased in (power); they have attained heaven by their greatness, and have made (for themselves) a spacious abode; may they, for whom Viс╣гс╣Зu defends (the sacrifice) that bestows all desires and confers delight, come (quickly), like birds, and sit down upon the plural asant and sacred grass.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those self-powerful ones strengthened themselves in their greatness. They mounted the vault; they made themselves a broad seat.
When Viс╣гс╣Зu rinsed the bull [=soma] arousing exhilaration,
[and/or] When Viс╣гс╣Зu aided the bull [=Indra], stirred by the
exhilarating drink,
they settled like birds on the dear ritual grass.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I tr. avardhanta as reflexive, rather than (with most tr.) intransitive тАШgrew strongтАЩ, in part because sv├бtavas- suggests that their power comes by their own efforts and in part because of its resonance with one interpretation of 1c, for which see above.

On p─Бda b see comments ad 6c and the similar phrase in 2b. The accent of the apparent main verb tasth├║с╕е is surprising. Macdonell (Reader) invokes the principle that the first of two antithetical verbs is accented, but this seems a feeble explanation of this particular situation. Ordinarily such antithetical verbs are adjacent to each other and the semantic antithesis is clearer: тАЬthey mountedтАЭ and тАЬthey madeтАЭ do not seem particularly antithetical. I see two possible explanations: either the ─Б╠БтАж tasth├║с╕е clause should be taken as an unmarked subordinate clause (тАЬ[when] they mounted the vault, they made тАжтАЭ) or the тАЬantitheticalтАЭ explanation is correct, but the verb to which it is antithetical is not the following cakrire. Instead it is found in 6c, whose two clauses are in patterned contrast to 7b: 6c s─л╠Бdat─Б╠Бbarh├нr ur├║ vah s├бdas kс╣Ыt├бm 7c ─Б╠Бn─Б╠Бkaс╣Г tasth├║r ur├║ cakrire s├бdaс╕е The second part of both p─Бdas contains ur├║ s├бdaс╕е тИЪkс╣Ы; the first parts contain the preverb ─Б╠Б, main verbs built to the semantically oppositional roots тИЪsad тАШsitтАЩ (s─л╠Бdata) and тИЪsth─Б тАШstandтАЩ (tasth├║с╕е), and an acc. of goal, again oppositional, in that the barh├нс╕е of 6c is on the earthly ritual ground and the n─Б╠Бkam is in heaven. I therefore think it likely that the accent on tasth├║с╕е is meant to signal the contrastive relationship between the two p─Бdas.

The Pp. analyses dh─Б╠Бvad as ha ─Б╠Бvat, and most tr. follow this interpretation, as containing an imperfect of тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ (Geldner тАЬAls Viс╣гс╣Зu dem тАж Bullen тАж beistandтАжтАЭ; Renou тАЬeut aid├йтАЭ; Macdonell тАЬhelpedтАЭ). (An injunctive ├бvat would also be possible.) However, we are likely dealing with a double, or even a triple, word play here, for dh─Б╠Бvat can also simply be the 3rd sg. injunctive belonging to the root (or rather roots) тИЪdh─Бv тАШrinseтАЩ and тАШrunтАЩ. This is recognized by Witzel Got┼Н, who translate with the second, тАЬAls Viс╣гс╣Зu zu dem vom Rausch bewegten Stier l├дuftтАж,тАЭ but in the notes also raise the possibility of тАШrinseтАЩ, referring to Got┼Н (Pr├дsensklasse p. 186 n. 333), who in turn refers to Pirart (IIJ 27 [1984] 102ff.).

I think that the two primary readings are тАЬrinsedтАЭ and тАЬaidedтАЭ and that the acc. object vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зaс╣Г madacy├║tam has different referents depending on the interpretation of the verb, namely soma and Indra respectively. This ambiguity is made possible by the fact that vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- тАШbullтАЩ is very commonly used of both Indra and soma. The modifying cmpd. madacy├║t- also has two different interpretations, enabled by the functional ambiguity of root noun compounds like this. Root noun second members regularly have transitive force, governing their first members, hence here тАЬarousing exhilaration.тАЭ And in fact this compound is common in this sense, modifying soma (IX.12.3, etc.). But passive value of the root noun with an instrumental or other oblique sense of the 1st member is also possible, hence here тАЬroused by the exhilarating drink / roused to exhilaration.тАЭ For general disc. see Scarlatta pp. 128- 29. In this second sense Indra would be the obvious referent, as he is elsewhere (e.g., I.51.2).

While тАШrinseтАЩ may strike the casual reader as an odd choice of words, in fact rinsing is one of the standard steps in the preparation of soma. For Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs participation in this process, see VI.17.11cd p┼лс╣г─Б╠Бv├нс╣гс╣Зus tr─л╠Бс╣Зi s├бr─Бс╣Гsi dh─Бvan, vrtrah├бnam mad ╠е ├нram aс╣Г┼Ы├║m asmai тАЬP┼лс╣гan, Viс╣гс╣Зu (and the others) rinse the exhilarating Vrtra ╠е -smashing plant, three lakes (full), for him [=Indra].тАЭ In the тАШaidedтАЩ interpretation, Indra is the referent of the accusative and the allusion is to Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs help given to him in various exploits including the Vс╣Ыtra-smashing. In the тАЬran toтАЭ reading, which strikes me as the least interesting, presumably Indra is also the referent of the accusative, though Witzel Got┼Н donтАЩt make this exactly clear.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLike heroes, like combatants, like men anxious for food, the swift-moving (Maruts) have engaged in battles; all beings fear the Maruts, who are the leaders (of the rain), and awful of aspect, like princes.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Like champions, like oncoming fighters, like those seeking fame in battles, they have marshaled themselves.
All creatures fear the MarutsтАФthe superior men glittering in appearance like kings.

+Griffith

In sooth like heroes fain for fight they rush about, like combatants fame-seeking have they striven in war.
Before the Maruts every creature is afraid: the men are like to Kings, terrible to behold.

+Geldner

Wie tapfere Krieger ausziehend, haben sie wie Ruhmbegierige in den K├дmpfen gewetteifert. Es f├╝rchten sich alle Wesen vor den Marut. Wie die K├╢nige sind die M├дnner von funkelndem Anblick.

+Grassmann

Kampflust’gen Helden gleich sind eilend sie, wie ruhmbegier’ge gehn in Schlachten sie geschart, Es f├╝rchten alle Wesen vor den Maruts sich, die M├дnner zeigen pr├дchtig sich wie K├╢nige.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, wields the well-made, golden, many-bladed thunderbolt, which the skillful Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б has framed for him, that he may achieve great exploits in war. He has slain Vс╣Ыtra and sent forth an ocean of water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б is agin the artisan of the gods

+Jamison Brereton

When Tvaс╣гс╣нar the good craftsman had turned the well-made golden mace with its thousand spikes,

Indra took it to do the manly works: he smashed Vr╠еtra, he forced out the flood of waters.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The array of tenses in this verse requires comment. The subordinate-main clause dyad of ab/c contains an imperfect ├бvartayat in the y├бd clause and a present dhatt├й (dhatt├б in sandhi) in the main clause. P─Бda d, which describes actions that necessarily follow the one in p─Бda c, then has two imperfects (├бhan and aubjat). I consider the imperfect / present combination in the first sentence to be a makeshift attempt to convey anteriority in a language without a semantic pluperfect. That is, there is no structural means in Rigvedic Sanskrit to convey past anterior action (тАЬwhen he had X-ed, he Y-edтАЭ) via a finite verb (though see recent work by Ian Hollenbaugh with a contrary opinion), since the тАЬpluperfectтАЭ is simply the past tense to presential perfects. In later Sanskrit the gerund serves as a non-finite way to express the value (тАЬhaving X-ed, he Y-edтАЭ), but the gerund barely exists in the RV. In the RV the perfect participle does serve this function, in contrast to finite forms of the perfect system. Here the relative tense values are conveyed by the imperfect followed by the present, since the imperfect does express action prior to that of the present tense. The imperfects in p─Бda d then re-establish the past-time context. I therefore tr. the imperfect and present of abc with the English pluperfect and preterite.

On n├бry ├бp─Бс╣Гsi see disc. ad VIII.96.19.

+Griffith

Als Tvaschtar kunstreich drechselte den goldnen Blitz, den sch├╢ngef├╝gten, welcher tausend Zacken hat, Da nahm ihn Indra, Mannesthaten zu vollziehn, erschlug den Vritra und ergoss der Wasser Flut.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBy their power, they bore the well aloft, and clove asunder the mountain that obstructed their path; the munificent Maruts, blowing upon their pipe, have conferred, when exhilarated by the Soma, desirable (gifts upon the sacrificer).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dhamanto v─Бс╣Зam = blowing upon their pipe;

V─Бс╣Зam = a lute, a v─лс╣З─Б with a hundred strings;

Dhamanta = blowing, applied to a pipe as a wind isntrument; avataс╕е avaс╣нaс╕е; avataс╕е k┼лpaс╕е (Nirukta 3.23.7)

+Jamison Brereton

They pushed the well upward with their power; they split apart the mountain, though it was firmly fixed.
Blowing their music, the Maruts of good drops performed these joyous (deeds) in the exhilaration of soma.

+Griffith

They with their vigorous strength pushed the well up on high, and clove the cloud in twain though it was passing strong.
The Maruts, bounteous Givers, sending forth their voice, in the wild joy of Soma wrought their glorious deeds.

+Geldner

Sie stie├Яen den Brunnen mit Kraft nach oben; sogar den festen Fels spalteten sie. Ihre Musik blasend haben die freigebigen Marut im Rausche des Soma erfreuliche Dinge verrichtet.

+Grassmann

Sie stiessen hoch den Brunnen mit Gewalt empor, zerschmetterten den festgef├╝gten Wolkenberg; Des Sturmes Pfeife blasend hat im Somarausch die reiche Schar der Maruts Herrliches vollbracht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey brought the crooked well to the plural ce (where the Muni was), and sprinkled the water upon the thirsty Gotama; the variously-radiant (Maruts) come to his succour, gratifyinng the desire of the sage with life-sustaining (waters).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: с╣Ъс╣гi Gotama, being thirsty, prayed to the Maruts for relief; Maruts brought a well from a distance to his hermitage

+Jamison Brereton

They pushed the well aslant in this way. They poured out the wellspring for the thirsting Gotama.
They come hither to him with helpтАФthey of bright radiance. They
satisfy the desire of the inspired poet through their own essential
qualities.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Oldenberg suggests a clever, but ultimately unsatisfactory, reading in p─Бda a: rather than t├бy─Б di┼Ы─Б╠Бwith the Pp., he divides t├б(y) ─Бd├н┼Ы─Б, with the instr. of ─Бd├н┼Ы- and the older sandhi form of t├й тАШtheyтАЩ. This would make the end of the p─Бda more parallel to 10a тАж t├б ├│jas─Б. He thinks that the Maruts performed the action in 10a with brute force, but that in 11a тАЬdurch klugen Anschlag.тАЭ Although I am drawn to this idea because of the persistent parallelisms in this hymn, I cannot accept it in the end. For one thing ─Бd├н┼Ы- does not occur in the instr., and it generally means тАШaim, intentionтАЩ, which does not fit here. OldenbergтАЩs proposed reading also involves altering the accent from di┼Ы─Б╠Бto ─Бd├н┼Ы─Б, so that it is not merely a matter of redividing the Saс╣Гhit─Б text. There is also the serious question of why t├бi╠пwould be preserved in one prevocalic environment but not in another, in adjacent vss.

The sequence ─Б╠Бgachant─лm in c appears to contain the 3rd pl. pres. gachanti + ─лm; this is certainly the default interpretation. However, as with vid├бnt─лm in I.67.4 and v├бrdhant─лm in I.65.4, I now think it should be analyzed as gachant + ─лm, an injunctive with the inherited *-ant ending preserved because it was early misanalyzed the primary ending fused with the enclitic pronoun ─лm. Vss. 11 relates how the Maruts brought rain to тАЬthirsting GotamaтАЭ; the first two p─Бdas contain preterities (pf.

nunudre, impf. ├бsi├▒can; note also vs. 10, devoted to the same theme, with 3 pfs.

nunudre, bibhiduс╕е, cakrire), while p─Бda d has the functionally ambiguous injunc.

tarpayanta. Only present gachanti intrudes. The published translation moves from past to present in vs. 11 (allowing for a presential reading of tarpayanta): тАЬThey pushed the well aslant in this way. They poured out the wellspring for the thirsting Gotama. / They come hither to him with help – they of bright radiance. They satisfy the desire of the inspired poet through their own essential qualities.тАЭ But the narrative sequence would flow better with тАЬthey came тАж they satisfied,тАЭ and I would emend the published translation accordingly. For this and other such passages (esp. I.65.4 and I.85.11), see my тАЬHidden in Plain Sight: Some Older Verb Endings in the Rig VedaтАЭ in a forthcoming festschrift.

+Griffith

They drave the cloud transverse directed hitherward, and poured the fountain forth for thirsting Gotama.
Shining with varied light they come to him with help: they with their might fulfilled the longing of the sage.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever blessings (are diffused) through the three worlds, and are in your gift, do you bestow upon the donor (of the oblation), who addressed you with praise; bestow them, also, Maruts, upon us, and grant us, bestowers of all good, riches, whence springs prosperity.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The shelters you have for the one who performs ritual laborтАФhold these out threefold to the pious man.
Extend these to us, Maruts; establish for us wealth in good heroes,
o bulls.

+Griffith

The shelters which ye have for him who lauds you, bestow them threefold on the man who offers.
Extend the same boons unto us, ye Maruts. Give us, O Heroes, wealth with noble offspring.
